│  labels are 1-3 word base terms like:                 ║ ║    rash, joint pain,  │

│  ║ ║  ALL modifiers go into separate fields (notes/location/etc).   ║ ║  If     │

│  recurrent, intermittent, constant, significant, debilitating, extreme,         │
│  excessive, noticeable, marked, notable, red, swollen, widespread, spotted,     │
│  dark, sharp, throbbing, crampy, dry, productive, concentrated, deep, dull      │
│  ── BANNED PATTERNS IN "name" FIELD ─────────────────────────────── "... with   │
│  ..."         → strip "with ..." to notes "... in <body part>"   → strip to     │
│  location "... on <body part>"   → strip to location "... reaching/peaking" →   │
│  strip to notes "... that ..."         → strip clause to notes "skin rash"      │
│  → use just "rash"                                                              │
│  ── DO NOT OVER-SPLIT TO BODY-PART WORDS ───────────────────────── Never        │
│  collapse a symptom phrase into only an anatomical noun. Forbidden:             │
│    "yellowing skin" → "skin"                                                    │
│    "yellow eyes" → "eyes"                                                       │
│    "joint pain" → "joint"                                                       │
│    "chest pain" → "chest"                                                       │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── REQUIRED MAPPINGS (use the RIGHT side as "name") ────────────── "skin rash  │
│  with red spots"   → "rash" "persistent joint pain"      → "joint pain"         │
│  "severe headache"            → "headache" "dry persistent cough"       →       │
│  "cough" "sharp abdominal pain"       → "abdominal pain" "dark concentrated     │
│  urine"    → "dark urine" "significant weight loss"    → "weight loss"          │
│  "excessive sweating"         → "sweating" "widespread skin rash"       →       │
│  "rash" "swollen lymph nodes in neck"→ "swollen lymph nodes" "yellowing skin"   │
│  → "yellow skin" "yellowish skin"             → "yellow skin" "yellowing of     │
│  skin"          → "yellow skin" "yellowing eyes"             → "yellow eyes"    │
│  "yellowing of eyes"          → "yellow eyes" "yellowing skin and eyes"    →    │
│  two entries: "yellow skin" + "yellow eyes"                                     │
│  These are ALWAYS valid as-is (do not simplify further): "loss of appetite",    │

│  of balance", "passage of gases", "internal itching", "burning micturition"     │
│  ── COMPOUND SPLITTING ──────────────────────────────────────────── "nausea     │
│  and vomiting" → two entries: "nausea" + "vomiting" "fever and chills"    →     │
│  two entries: "fever" + "chills" "yellowing skin and eyes" → two entries:       │
│  "yellow skin" + "yellow eyes" "yellow skin and eyes" → two entries: "yellow    │
│  skin" + "yellow eyes"                                                          │
│  ── MANDATORY SELF-CHECK (before output) ────────────────────────── For EVERY   │
│  symptom in your output, verify:                                                │

│                                                                                 │
│  Agent: Clinical Workflow Orchestrator                                          │
│                                                                                 │
│  Task: You will receive a list of symptoms from the extract_symptoms_task       │
│  output.                                                                        │
│  CRITICAL TOOL CONTRACT: graphdb_ontology_query only executes the exact         │
│  sparql_query you send. It does not determine intent or compose query logic     │
│  for you. You must decide what to query and build the query. Use the            │
│  graphdb_ontology_query tool description as the source of query-construction    │
│  guidance.                                                                      │
│  Process ALL symptoms in a single pass. For each symptom:                       │
│  Step 0 - Normalize symptom text before querying: Preserve clinically           │
│  meaningful multi-word phrases and never collapse to anatomy-only terms.        │
│  Forbidden: "yellowing skin" → "skin" If a phrase combines shared qualifier +   │
│  two locations, split it into two normalized symptoms before mapping:           │
│    "yellowing skin and eyes" → "yellow skin" + "yellow eyes"                    │
│                                                                                 │
│  Step 1 - Search query authoring: Build a read-only ontology lookup query that  │
│  searches SYMP entities by symptom label text using case-insensitive matching.  │
│  Ensure the query returns both term URI and label so you can choose the best    │
│  candidate.                                                                     │
│  Step 2 - Retrieve ontology results: Call graphdb_ontology_query directly with  │
│  a read-only label-search SPARQL query for each symptom. Read candidate URIs,   │
│  labels, and parsed IDs from tool output.                                       │
│  Step 3 - Select best candidate by semantic label relevance. If no relevant     │
│  candidate is found, proceed to Step 4.                                         │
│  Step 4 - Retry with PROGRESSIVE SIMPLIFICATION (mandatory before unmapped):    │
│  ★★★ RETRY STRATEGY — FOLLOW IN ORDER ★★★                                       │
│  Retry A — Drop qualifiers: If the symptom name still contains adjectives or    │
│  modifiers, strip them and search again.                                        │
│    "persistent joint pain" → search "joint pain"                                │
│    "severe headache" → search "headache"                                        │
│    "skin rash" → search "rash"                                                  │
│    "dark concentrated urine" → search "dark urine", then "urine"                │
│    "burning micturition" → search "micturition", then "dysuria"                 │
│                                                                                 │
│  Retry B — Try the root/base term only:                                         │
│    "joint pain" → search "pain" (if "joint pain" returned nothing)              │
│    "muscle weakness" → search "weakness"                                        │
│    "swollen lymph nodes" → search "lymph" or "lymphadenopathy"                  │
│    "chest tightness" → search "tightness"                                       │
│                                                                                 │
│                                                                                 │
│                                                                                 │
│  You MUST attempt at least 2 retries using different simplification or synonym  │
│  strategies before proceeding to the HP ontology fallback.                      │
│  Retry C — HP Ontology Fallback (mandatory before marking unmapped): If         │
│  Retries A and B all failed to find a SYMP match, use the hp_ontology_query     │
│  tool to search the Human Phenotype (HP) Ontology for the symptom term. The HP  │
│  ontology uses different terminology and may recognize terms that SYMP does     │
│  not directly index.                                                            │
│  Steps for Retry C:                                                             │
│    C1. Call hp_ontology_query with the original symptom name:                   │
│        {"search_term": "<symptom name>"}                                        │
│                                                                                 │
│    C2. Read the response. Look at the suggested_symp_search_terms list.         │
│        These are HP ontology labels that describe the same or related           │
│        phenotype using alternative terminology.                                 │
│                                                                                 │
│    C3. For EACH suggested term in suggested_symp_search_terms (try up to 3),    │
│        call graphdb_ontology_query with a PATTERN 1 (label search) query        │
│        using the HP-suggested label as the search text.                         │
│                                                                                 │
│    C4. If any of these SYMP searches return a match, select the best            │
│        candidate and use it as the mapping. You are done for this symptom.      │
│                                                                                 │
│    C5. If hp_ontology_query returned no suggestions, or none of the             │
│        HP-suggested terms matched in SYMP either, THEN mark as unmapped.        │
│                                                                                 │
│  Example:                                                                       │
│    - SYMP search "passage of gases" → no results                                │
│    - Retry A/B/C: "gases", "gas", "flatulence" → still nothing in SYMP          │
│    - hp_ontology_query({"search_term": "passage of gases"})                     │
│      → suggested_symp_search_terms: ["flatulence", "increased flatus"]          │
│    - SYMP search "flatulence" → FOUND SYMP match! Use it.                       │
│                                                                                 │
│  Example:                                                                       │
│    - SYMP search "spinning movements" → no results                              │
│    - Retry A/B: "spinning", "vertigo", "dizziness" → still nothing              │
│    - hp_ontology_query({"search_term": "spinning movements"})                   │
│      → suggested_symp_search_terms: ["vertigo", "dizziness"]                    │
│    - SYMP search "vertigo" → FOUND! Use it.                                     │
│                                                                                 │
│  CRITICAL RULES for Retry C: - HP URIs are NOT SYMP URIs. NEVER use an HP URI   │
│  as the matched_symp_uri. - Use HP labels ONLY as alternative search terms for  │
│  SYMP lookups. - The final matched_symp_uri, matched_symp_label, and            │
│  parsed_symp_number                                                             │
│    MUST come from a graphdb_ontology_query (SYMP) response, not from HP.        │
│  - You MUST attempt Retry C before marking any symptom as unmapped.             │
│  Step 5 - Use parsed_symp_number from the selected candidate. If missing,       │
│  parse only digits after SYMP_ from the selected URI.                           │
│  Step 6 - Repeat for the next symptom until all are processed.                  │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - You MUST use tool-backed ontology evidence for every         │
│  symptom. - matched_symp_uri and matched_symp_label MUST come from tool         │
│  responses only. - NEVER reduce a symptom to an anatomy-only word (e.g.,        │
│  "skin", "eyes", "joint"). - NEVER invent, guess, or assume any SYMP URI,       │
│  label, or numeric ID. - If tools return no results after all retries           │
│  INCLUDING the HP ontology                                                      │
│    fallback (Retry C), set status "unmapped" and set matched_symp_uri,          │
│    matched_symp_label, parsed_symp_number all to null.                          │
│  - An unmapped result with null values is always correct over any fabrication.  │
│  - You MUST attempt the HP ontology fallback (Retry C) before marking           │
│  unmapped.                                                                      │

│  object:                                                                        │
│    {"sparql_query": "<full query string>"}                                      │
│  - Call hp_ontology_query with a flat object:                                   │
│    {"search_term": "<symptom text>"}                                            │
│  - If tool fails, retry up to 2 times before unmapped.                          │

│  CRITICAL TOOL CONTRACT: graphdb_ontology_query only runs the exact             │
│  sparql_query payload you provide. It does not infer intent, fill missing       │
│  parts, or generate a query for you. You must decide query intent and author    │
│  the query. Use the graphdb_ontology_query tool description for                 │
│  query-construction rules.                                                      │
│  For each entry in symp_mappings, follow EXACTLY one of these two cases:        │
│  CASE A - status is "unmapped" OR parsed_symp_number is null or empty:          │
│    Do NOT call any tool.                                                        │
│    Record this entry with disease_candidates set to [] and status "skipped".    │
│                                                                                 │
│  CASE B - status is "mapped" AND parsed_symp_number is a non-empty digit        │
│  string:                                                                        │
│    You have to call the tool to find associated diseases for this known         │
│  symptom.                                                                       │
│    Find diseases linked to a known symptom by calling graphdb_ontology_query    │
│  tool.                                                                          │
│                                                                                 │
│    Use EXACTLY this SPARQL query. Replace ONLY <SYMPTOM_URI_PLACEHOLDER> with   │
│  the actual                                                                     │
│    matched_symp_uri value in angle brackets (e.g.                               │
│  <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/SYMP_0000457>).                                │
│    Do NOT change anything else in the query — not the variable names, not the   │
│  property, not the structure.                                                   │
│                                                                                 │
│    PREFIX owl:  <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#>                                │
│    PREFIX rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#>                         │
│    PREFIX ro:   <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/RO_>                            │
│    SELECT ?disease ?diseaseLabel                                                │
│    WHERE {                                                                      │
│      ?disease rdfs:subClassOf ?restriction .                                    │
│      ?restriction owl:onProperty ro:0002452 .                                   │
│      ?restriction owl:someValuesFrom <SYMPTOM_URI_PLACEHOLDER> .                │
│      ?disease rdfs:label ?diseaseLabel .                                        │
│      FILTER(LANG(?diseaseLabel) = "en")                                         │
│    }                                                                            │
│                                                                                 │
│    Call graphdb_ontology_query with:                                            │
│    {"sparql_query": "<the query above with the real URI substituted>"}          │
│                                                                                 │
│    Read the "disease_candidates"                                                │
│    array from tool result. Copy every string verbatim into                      │
│    this entry's disease_candidates. Do not modify any string.                   │
│                                                                                 │
│    Also parse "disease_rows" from the same response. For each row,              │
│    copy disease URI and label exactly as returned into disease_entries.         │
│    Prefer row.disease_uri if present, otherwise row.disease_iri.                │
│                                                                                 │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - disease_candidates must contain ONLY strings from the tool   │
│  response. - disease_entries must contain ONLY URI/label pairs from tool        │
│  response rows. - NEVER invent, guess, infer, or paraphrase any disease name.   │
│  - NEVER use symptom names as disease names. - NEVER copy disease names from    │
│  examples, instructions, or memory. - If the tool returns an empty              │
│  "disease_candidates" array, record []                                          │

│                                                                                 │
│  Task Started                                                                   │
│  Name: rank_diagnoses_task                                                      │
│  ID: 0ac483b5-36d7-499f-aeec-eed4b866a998                                       │
│                                                                                 │

╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

╭─────────────────────────────── 🤖 Agent Started ────────────────────────────────╮
│                                                                                 │
│  Agent: Clinical Workflow Orchestrator                                          │
│                                                                                 │
│  Task: You will receive the disease_results list from the                       │
│  query_diseases_for_symptoms_task output.                                       │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  IMPROVED SCORING ALGORITHM — TF-IDF-INSPIRED DIFFERENTIAL DIAGNOSIS            │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  The simple co-occurrence count treats all symptom matches equally, but a       │
│  match on "fatigue" (linked to 60+ diseases) is far less informative than a     │
│  match on "rusty sputum" (linked to 2-3 diseases). This algorithm fixes that    │
│  by weighting each symptom match by its SPECIFICITY.                            │
│  ── Step 1: Count disease frequency per symptom (IDF) ──────────────            │
│  For each mapped symptom S in disease_results:                                  │
│    disease_count[S] = number of unique diseases in S.disease_candidates         │
│                                                                                 │
│  This tells you how "common" or "rare" each symptom is across diseases. A       │
│  symptom linked to many diseases is non-specific (low diagnostic value). A      │
│  symptom linked to few diseases is highly specific (high diagnostic value).     │
│  ── Step 2: Compute specificity weight per symptom ─────────────────            │
│  For each mapped symptom S:                                                     │
│    If disease_count[S] == 0: skip (no diseases found for this symptom)          │
│    Else: specificity_weight[S] = 1.0 / log2(1 + disease_count[S])               │
│                                                                                 │
│  Examples (approximate):                                                        │
│    - Symptom linked to 1 disease:   weight = 1.0 / log2(2)   = 1.000            │
│    - Symptom linked to 3 diseases:  weight = 1.0 / log2(4)   = 0.500            │
│    - Symptom linked to 7 diseases:  weight = 1.0 / log2(8)   = 0.333            │
│    - Symptom linked to 15 diseases: weight = 1.0 / log2(16)  = 0.250            │
│    - Symptom linked to 63 diseases: weight = 1.0 / log2(64)  = 0.167            │
│                                                                                 │
│  This means a match on a rare symptom contributes ~6x more to the score than a  │
│  match on a very common symptom.                                                │
│  ── Step 3: Build disease scores ───────────────────────────────────            │
│  Let total_mapped_symptoms = count of symptoms with status != "skipped"         │
│                              AND disease_count[S] > 0                           │
│                                                                                 │
│  For each unique disease D found in any disease_candidates list:                │
│    matching_symptoms[D] = list of symptom names where D appears                 │
│    raw_score[D] = SUM of specificity_weight[S] for each S in                    │
│  matching_symptoms[D]                                                           │
│    match_count[D] = number of distinct symptoms D matched (old co-occurrence    │
│  count)                                                                         │
│    coverage[D] = match_count[D] / total_mapped_symptoms                         │
│                                                                                 │
│    ★ composite_score[D] = raw_score[D] × (0.5 + 0.5 × coverage[D])              │
│                                                                                 │
│  The coverage multiplier ranges from 0.5 (matches only 1 symptom) to 1.0        │
│  (matches all symptoms). This means: - A disease matching 8/10 symptoms with    │
│  moderate specificity beats                                                     │
│    a disease matching 2/10 symptoms with high specificity.                      │
│  - But a disease matching 2/10 highly specific symptoms still beats             │
│    a disease matching 3/10 very common symptoms.                                │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 4: Rank ───────────────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  Sort diseases by composite_score descending. Break ties by match_count         │
│  descending. Break further ties alphabetically. Assign rank starting from 1.    │
│  ★ OUTPUT LIMIT: Return ONLY the top 20 diseases. Diseases ranked 21+ are       │
│  noise and should be omitted from the output entirely.                          │
│  ── Step 5: Assign confidence tiers ────────────────────────────────            │
│  Let top_score = composite_score of rank-1 disease.                             │
│  For each disease D:                                                            │
│    HIGH   — composite_score[D] ≥ 0.7 × top_score AND match_count[D] ≥ 3         │
│    MEDIUM — composite_score[D] ≥ 0.4 × top_score AND match_count[D] ≥ 2         │
│    LOW    — everything else                                                     │
│                                                                                 │
│  Special case: if top_score < 0.5 (very weak evidence overall), cap all         │
│  confidences at MEDIUM and add a note about weak evidence.                      │
│  ── Step 6: For each ranked disease, list supporting symptoms ──────            │
│  For each disease in the output, include:                                       │
│    - supporting_symptoms: list of symptom names that matched                    │
│    - Each symptom annotated with its specificity_weight (rounded to 3           │
│  decimals)                                                                      │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 7: Return the differential diagnosis report ───────────────            │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - Only include diseases that appear in disease_results         │
│  disease_candidates lists. - NEVER add diseases from your own medical           │
│  knowledge or memory. - NEVER invent or infer any disease not present in the    │
│  input data. - If all disease_candidates lists are empty, return an empty       │
│    differential_diagnosis list and explain in notes. Do not fabricate.          │
│  - An empty diagnosis is always correct over a fabricated one. - Use log2       │
│  (base-2 logarithm) for all specificity calculations. - Round all scores to 3   │
│  decimal places in the output.                                                  │
│  CALCULATION VERIFICATION: Before outputting, verify at least one example       │
│  disease by hand:                                                               │
│    1. List its matching symptoms                                                │
│    2. Look up each symptom's disease_count                                      │
│    3. Compute each specificity_weight = 1/log2(1+disease_count)                 │
│    4. Sum them → raw_score                                                      │
│    5. Compute coverage = match_count / total_mapped_symptoms                    │
│    6. composite_score = raw_score × (0.5 + 0.5 × coverage)                      │
│  If the computed value doesn't match your output, fix it.                       │
│                                                                                 │
│                                                                                 │
╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

╭─────────────────────────────── 🤖 Agent Started ────────────────────────────────╮
│                                                                                 │
│  Agent: Clinical Workflow Orchestrator                                          │
│                                                                                 │
│  Task: You will receive disease_results and differential_diagnosis from prior   │
│  tasks.                                                                         │
│  CRITICAL TOOL CONTRACT: graphdb_ontology_query is only an execution layer. It  │
│  executes the exact sparql_query string you send and nothing else. You must     │
│  decide what data is needed and author the query accordingly. Use the           │
│  graphdb_ontology_query tool description to construct valid queries.            │
│  ── TRIGGER RULE ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── If  │
│  total_diseases_found <= 1:                                                     │
│    Set followup_needed = false. Return empty disease_symptom_profiles and       │
│    questions_asked arrays immediately. Do not call any tools.                   │
│  If total_diseases_found > 1:                                                   │
│    Follow-up is MANDATORY. Continue with the steps below.                       │
│  ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────     │
│  Step 1 - Select candidate diseases for profiling.                              │
│    Take all diseases with HIGH or MEDIUM confidence from                        │
│  differential_diagnosis.                                                        │
│    Also include any LOW-confidence diseases whose co_occurrence_score equals    │
│    the highest co_occurrence_score present (ties at the top).                   │
│    Cap the candidate set at 5 diseases.                                         │
│                                                                                 │
│  Step 2 - Fetch symptom profiles.                                               │
│    For each candidate disease, locate its disease_uri in disease_entries        │
│    (from disease_results). If no URI is available, mark it                      │
│  skipped_for_followup.                                                          │
│    For every disease with a URI:                                                │
│    a) Copy PATTERN 2 (disease-to-symptom) from graphdb_ontology_query tool      │
│  description.                                                                   │
│    b) Replace <disease_uri> with the actual disease URI.                        │
│    c) Execute it using graphdb_ontology_query with {"sparql_query": "<full      │
│  query string>"}.                                                               │
│    d) Do NOT add FILTER(LANG(...)) or any other filters to the pattern.         │
│    e) Collect the returned symptom labels into that disease's                   │
│  candidate_symptoms list.                                                       │
│    f) Use tool output only; never fabricate symptom labels.                     │
│                                                                                 │
│  Step 3 - Build a global discriminative symptom pool.                           │
│    Collect every symptom label across all profiled diseases into one pool.      │
│    Then apply these filters IN ORDER:                                           │
│      a) Remove symptoms already present in the initial patient message          │
│         (case-insensitive match against the original extracted symptom names).  │
│      b) Remove symptoms that appear in ALL candidate disease profiles           │
│         (they cannot discriminate between diseases).                            │
│      c) Score each remaining symptom by discriminative power:                   │
│           score = (number of candidate diseases that do NOT list this symptom)  │
│           Higher score = more exclusive to fewer diseases = more                │
│  discriminative.                                                                │
│      d) Break ties by preferring symptoms linked to higher-ranked diseases      │
│         (lower rank number = higher priority).                                  │
│                                                                                 │
│  Step 4 - Select questions.                                                     │
│    Select an adaptive number of symptoms from highest discriminative score,     │
│    asking as few questions as possible while still separating top diagnoses.    │
│    Maximum allowed patient questions: 22.                                       │
│                                                                                 │
│    ★★★ MANDATORY CLASSIFICATION BEFORE ASKING ★★★                               │
│    STEP A: Classify each selected symptom.                                      │
│    Apply REASONING (not hardcoded lists) to classify each selected symptom as   │
│  EITHER:                                                                        │
│    - investigation_required, OR                                                 │
│    - patient_reportable                                                         │
│                                                                                 │
│    INVESTIGATION_REQUIRED classification rule:                                  │
│    Apply these checks IN ORDER. If ANY apply, classify as                       │
│  investigation_required:                                                        │
│    1. Does it require specialized equipment to detect? (BP cuff, oximeter,      │
│  ECG, lab machine, imaging)                                                     │
│    2. Is it a measurement/lab value? (e.g., "120/80 mmHg", "glucose 95 mg/dL",  │
│  "WBC 5K")                                                                      │
│    3. Is it a biomarker or lab finding? (enzymes, counts, levels, CRP, liver    │
│  function tests)                                                                │
│    4. Is it an imaging/radiology result? (X-ray/CT/MRI/ultrasound findings)     │
│    5. Does it require professional clinical assessment? (heart murmurs          │
│  detected by stethoscope,                                                       │
│       retinal findings, some skin signs requiring magnification)                │
│    6. Does the symptom name contain measurement keywords? (pressure,            │
│  saturation, heart rate,                                                        │
│       count, enzyme, level, finding, imaging, ECG, EKG, result, test)           │
│                                                                                 │
│    PATIENT_REPORTABLE classification rule:                                      │
│    Apply these checks. If ANY apply, classify as patient_reportable:            │
│    1. Patient directly feels/experiences it? (fever/feeling hot,                │
│  cough/coughing, pain/hurt,                                                     │
│       nausea/feeling sick, dizziness/feeling faint, fatigue/tiredness)          │
│    2. Patient can directly observe it? (bleeding they see, rash/spots they      │
│  see, swelling they feel)                                                       │
│    3. Patient can describe it without equipment? (Yes = patient_reportable)     │
│    4. It's a subjective symptom or patient-observable sign? (Yes =              │
│  patient_reportable)                                                            │
│                                                                                 │
│    ★★★ MANDATORY SEPARATION STEP ★★★                                            │
│    STEP B: Create TWO SEPARATE LISTS after classification:                      │
│    List_A = all symptoms classified as investigation_required                   │
│    List_B = all symptoms classified as patient_reportable                       │
│                                                                                 │
│    THEN:                                                                        │
│    - Add ALL items from List_A to investigations_required with a reason         │
│    - Use ONLY List_B to generate patient questions                              │
│    - NEVER generate a question for anything in List_A                           │
│                                                                                 │
│    ★★★ MANDATORY FILTERING RULE ★★★                                             │
│    - investigation_required items DO NOT become patient questions.              │
│    - investigation_required items MUST be added to investigations_required      │
│  list with a brief reason.                                                      │
│    - Only patient_reportable items may become yes/no questions.                 │
│    - If a symptom appears in questions_asked, it MUST be verified as in List_B  │
│  (patient_reportable).                                                          │
│    - AUDIT: No symptom should appear in BOTH questions_asked AND                │
│  investigations_required.                                                       │
│                                                                                 │
│    For patient_reportable items ONLY (from List_B), create yes/no questions:    │
│    For each selected symptom in List_B, emit exactly one yes/no question using  │
│  this                                                                           │
│    conditional style:                                                           │
│    - If the symptom is a common everyday term (e.g., fever, cough, headache),   │
│      ask directly: "Do you have <symptom>?"                                     │
│    - Treat these as common everyday terms and ask directly with no              │
│      parentheses: fever, cough, headache, bleeding, vomiting, diarrhea,         │
│      chest pain, sore throat, muscle pain, joint pain.                          │
│    - If the symptom is a medical/technical term (e.g., rash, dysuria,           │
│      dyspnea), ask with a plain explanation plus the term in parentheses:       │
│      "Do you have <simple explanation> (<medical term>)?"                       │
│      Example: "Do you have red spots on the skin (rash)?"                       │
│                                                                                 │
│    If needed for grammar, a close equivalent is allowed, but it MUST remain     │
│    a single yes/no question about exactly one symptom.                          │
│    Keep each question short (max 14 words), patient-friendly, and avoid         │
│    medical jargon unless it is part of the symptom label.                       │
│    Do not ask severity, duration, or cause in the same question.                │
│    IMPORTANT language policy:                                                   │
│    - Use easy, non-technical wording so any patient can understand.             │
│    - Include parentheses only when the symptom label is medical/technical.      │
│    - Common everyday symptom names should NOT be rewritten with parentheses.    │
│    - Example common: "Do you have fever?"                                       │
│    - Example common: "Do you have bleeding?"                                    │
│    - Example medical: "Do you have yellow skin or eyes (jaundice)?"             │
│    - The wording before parentheses MUST explain the symptom in plain words,    │
│      not repeat the same medical label.                                         │
│    - FORBIDDEN example: "Do you have rash (rash)?"                              │
│    - FORBIDDEN example: "Do you have bleeding (bleeding)?"                      │
│    - CORRECT example: "Do you have red or itchy skin spots (rash)?"             │
│    Global deduplication: never emit the same symptom question twice.            │
│    Skip any symptom that already has a non-empty patient_answer in the          │
│    input context.                                                               │
│                                                                                 │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - Call graphdb_ontology_query ONLY with SPARQL queries built   │
│  from URIs in disease_entries. - Never invent disease URIs, symptom URIs, or    │
│  symptom labels. - Never ask about a symptom the patient already confirmed.     │
│  ★★★ CRITICAL: Copy SPARQL patterns EXACTLY from graphdb_ontology_query tool    │
│  description. ★★★ CRITICAL: Do NOT add FILTER(LANG(...)) or any filters NOT     │
│  shown in the patterns. ★★★ CRITICAL: Deviating from patterns = zero results =  │
│  failed queries. Follow patterns exactly. ★★★ CRITICAL: Use reasoning—not       │
│  hardcoded lists—to classify each symptom as investigation_required or          │
│  patient_reportable. ★★★ CRITICAL: Create TWO SEPARATE LISTS after              │
│  classification (investigation_required and patient_reportable). ★★★ CRITICAL:  │
│  investigation_required symptoms MUST NOT appear in questions_asked under ANY   │
│  circumstance. ★★★ CRITICAL: Do NOT ask about hypotension, shock,               │
│  thrombocytopenia, or ANY investigation_required finding. ★★★ CRITICAL: AUDIT   │
│  your output: if any symptom appears in BOTH questions_asked and                │
│  investigations_required, the output is WRONG. - Any symptom requiring          │
│  equipment/measurement/labs/imaging to detect MUST be investigation_required.   │
│  - Any symptom the patient can directly experience or observe without           │
│  equipment is patient_reportable. - If uncertain about a symptom's nature,      │
│  apply the classification rules above; do not guess. - Never produce or         │
│  suggest a final diagnosis in this step. - questions_asked must contain no      │
│  duplicate symptom entries. - Each question in questions_asked must end with    │
│  "?" and be answerable by yes/no only. - Each question must reference exactly   │
│  one symptom from candidate_symptoms. - For medical/technical symptoms,         │
│  include the medical term in parentheses. - For common symptoms, do not add     │
│  parentheses unless needed for clarity. - Never output "<term> (<term>)" for    │
│  any symptom. - Every symptom in questions_asked must be verified as            │
│  patient_reportable (not investigation_required).                               │
│                                                                                 │

╭─────────────────────────── 🚀 Crew Execution Started ───────────────────────────╮
│                                                                                 │
│  Crew Execution Started                                                         │
│  Name: crew                                                                     │
│  ID: 0d4d966e-51eb-403b-8556-2f16f4b62159                                       │
│                                                                                 │
│                                                                                 │
╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

╭──────────────────────────────── 📋 Task Started ────────────────────────────────╮
│                                                                                 │
│  Task Started                                                                   │
│  Name: You will receive the initial differential_diagnosis and the completed    │
│  questions_asked list with patient_answer fields filled in by the patient,      │
│  both provided as JSON blocks appended below this description by the runtime.   │
│  Also available: the disease_symptom_profiles list (which disease has which     │
│  candidate symptoms) from the follow-up payload.                                │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  WEIGHTED REFINEMENT SCORING ALGORITHM                                          │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  This algorithm uses the improved composite_score from Phase 1 as the baseline  │
│  score, then applies WEIGHTED follow-up evidence adjustments. Follow-up         │
│  symptoms that are more discriminative (appear in fewer candidate disease       │
│  profiles) carry more weight.                                                   │
│  ── Step 1: Compute discriminative weight for each follow-up symptom ──         │
│  Let N = number of diseases in disease_symptom_profiles with status "profiled"  │
│  For each question Q in questions_asked:                                        │
│    diseases_with_symptom = count of profiled diseases whose candidate_symptoms  │
│                            list contains Q.symptom (case-insensitive)           │
│    If diseases_with_symptom == 0: discriminative_weight = 0 (skip)              │
│    Else: discriminative_weight[Q.symptom] = 1.0 - (diseases_with_symptom / N)   │
│                                                                                 │
│  Examples with 5 profiled diseases:                                             │
│    - Symptom appears in 1/5 diseases: weight = 0.8 (highly discriminative)      │
│    - Symptom appears in 2/5 diseases: weight = 0.6                              │
│    - Symptom appears in 3/5 diseases: weight = 0.4                              │
│    - Symptom appears in 5/5 diseases: weight = 0.0 (not discriminative at all)  │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 2: Compute adjustments for each disease ───────────────────            │
│  For every disease D in initial differential_diagnosis:                         │
│    baseline = D.composite_score (from Phase 1)                                  │
│    support_delta = 0.0                                                          │
│    conflict_delta = 0.0                                                         │
│                                                                                 │
│    For each question Q in questions_asked:                                      │
│      Normalize answer: Q.patient_answer.strip().lower()                         │
│      w = discriminative_weight[Q.symptom] (or 0 if not computed)                │
│                                                                                 │
│      If answer is "yes" or starts with "yes":                                   │
│        If disease D's candidate_symptoms list contains Q.symptom:               │
│          support_delta += w    (weighted support)                               │
│                                                                                 │
│      If answer is "no" or starts with "no":                                     │
│        If disease D's candidate_symptoms list contains Q.symptom:               │
│          conflict_delta += w   (weighted conflict)                              │
│                                                                                 │
│      Any other answer → neutral, no change.                                     │
│                                                                                 │
│    final_score[D] = baseline + support_delta - conflict_delta                   │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 3: Re-rank ────────────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  Sort diseases by final_score descending. Break ties by match_count descending  │
│  (from Phase 1). Break further ties alphabetically. Renumber ranks starting     │
│  from 1.                                                                        │
│  ── Step 4: Confidence assignment ──────────────────────────────────            │
│  Let top_score = final_score of rank-1 disease,                                 │
│      second_score = final_score of rank-2 disease (or 0 if only one disease).   │
│      gap = top_score - second_score                                             │
│                                                                                 │
│  Rank-1 disease:                                                                │
│    HIGH   — gap ≥ 0.5 × top_score, or only one disease remains                  │
│    MEDIUM — gap > 0 but < 0.5 × top_score                                       │
│    LOW    — gap == 0 (still tied after all evidence)                            │
│                                                                                 │
│  All other diseases:                                                            │
│    MEDIUM — final_score > 0.5 × top_score                                       │
│    LOW    — otherwise                                                           │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 5: Transparency ───────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  For each disease in the output, reasoning must explicitly state:               │
│    - Baseline composite_score from Phase 1                                      │
│    - Which follow-up symptoms were confirmed (yes) and their weights            │
│    - Which follow-up symptoms were denied (no) and their weights                │
│    - Net adjustment: +support_delta - conflict_delta                            │
│    - How the rank changed vs Phase 1 (e.g. "moved from rank 3 to rank 1")       │
│                                                                                 │
│  followup_summary must name the single most impactful answer (highest weight    │
│  confirmed or denied) and explain why it shifted the ranking.                   │
│  If ALL patient answers were neutral, set notes to:                             │
│    "All follow-up answers were neutral; ranking unchanged from baseline."       │
│                                                                                 │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - Only diseases present in initial differential_diagnosis may  │
│  appear in output. - Never invent new diseases or symptoms. - Use follow-up     │
│  answers as the ONLY post-baseline evidence source. - An unchanged ranking      │
│  with an honest explanation is always correct. - Round all scores to 3 decimal  │
│  places.                                                                        │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── INITIAL RANKING (JSON) ──────────────────────────────────────               │

╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

╭─────────────────────────────── 🤖 Agent Started ────────────────────────────────╮
│                                                                                 │
│  Agent: Final Diagnostic Reasoning Specialist                                   │
│                                                                                 │
│  Task: You will receive the initial differential_diagnosis and the completed    │
│  questions_asked list with patient_answer fields filled in by the patient,      │
│  both provided as JSON blocks appended below this description by the runtime.   │
│  Also available: the disease_symptom_profiles list (which disease has which     │
│  candidate symptoms) from the follow-up payload.                                │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  WEIGHTED REFINEMENT SCORING ALGORITHM                                          │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  This algorithm uses the improved composite_score from Phase 1 as the baseline  │
│  score, then applies WEIGHTED follow-up evidence adjustments. Follow-up         │
│  symptoms that are more discriminative (appear in fewer candidate disease       │
│  profiles) carry more weight.                                                   │
│  ── Step 1: Compute discriminative weight for each follow-up symptom ──         │
│  Let N = number of diseases in disease_symptom_profiles with status "profiled"  │
│  For each question Q in questions_asked:                                        │
│    diseases_with_symptom = count of profiled diseases whose candidate_symptoms  │
│                            list contains Q.symptom (case-insensitive)           │
│    If diseases_with_symptom == 0: discriminative_weight = 0 (skip)              │
│    Else: discriminative_weight[Q.symptom] = 1.0 - (diseases_with_symptom / N)   │
│                                                                                 │
│  Examples with 5 profiled diseases:                                             │
│    - Symptom appears in 1/5 diseases: weight = 0.8 (highly discriminative)      │
│    - Symptom appears in 2/5 diseases: weight = 0.6                              │
│    - Symptom appears in 3/5 diseases: weight = 0.4                              │
│    - Symptom appears in 5/5 diseases: weight = 0.0 (not discriminative at all)  │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 2: Compute adjustments for each disease ───────────────────            │
│  For every disease D in initial differential_diagnosis:                         │
│    baseline = D.composite_score (from Phase 1)                                  │
│    support_delta = 0.0                                                          │
│    conflict_delta = 0.0                                                         │
│                                                                                 │
│    For each question Q in questions_asked:                                      │
│      Normalize answer: Q.patient_answer.strip().lower()                         │
│      w = discriminative_weight[Q.symptom] (or 0 if not computed)                │
│                                                                                 │
│      If answer is "yes" or starts with "yes":                                   │
│        If disease D's candidate_symptoms list contains Q.symptom:               │
│          support_delta += w    (weighted support)                               │
│                                                                                 │
│      If answer is "no" or starts with "no":                                     │
│        If disease D's candidate_symptoms list contains Q.symptom:               │
│          conflict_delta += w   (weighted conflict)                              │
│                                                                                 │
│      Any other answer → neutral, no change.                                     │
│                                                                                 │
│    final_score[D] = baseline + support_delta - conflict_delta                   │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 3: Re-rank ────────────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  Sort diseases by final_score descending. Break ties by match_count descending  │
│  (from Phase 1). Break further ties alphabetically. Renumber ranks starting     │
│  from 1.                                                                        │
│  ── Step 4: Confidence assignment ──────────────────────────────────            │
│  Let top_score = final_score of rank-1 disease,                                 │
│      second_score = final_score of rank-2 disease (or 0 if only one disease).   │
│      gap = top_score - second_score                                             │
│                                                                                 │
│  Rank-1 disease:                                                                │
│    HIGH   — gap ≥ 0.5 × top_score, or only one disease remains                  │
│    MEDIUM — gap > 0 but < 0.5 × top_score                                       │
│    LOW    — gap == 0 (still tied after all evidence)                            │
│                                                                                 │
│  All other diseases:                                                            │
│    MEDIUM — final_score > 0.5 × top_score                                       │
│    LOW    — otherwise                                                           │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 5: Transparency ───────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  For each disease in the output, reasoning must explicitly state:               │
│    - Baseline composite_score from Phase 1                                      │
│    - Which follow-up symptoms were confirmed (yes) and their weights            │
│    - Which follow-up symptoms were denied (no) and their weights                │
│    - Net adjustment: +support_delta - conflict_delta                            │
│    - How the rank changed vs Phase 1 (e.g. "moved from rank 3 to rank 1")       │
│                                                                                 │
│  followup_summary must name the single most impactful answer (highest weight    │
│  confirmed or denied) and explain why it shifted the ranking.                   │
│  If ALL patient answers were neutral, set notes to:                             │
│    "All follow-up answers were neutral; ranking unchanged from baseline."       │
│                                                                                 │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - Only diseases present in initial differential_diagnosis may  │
│  appear in output. - Never invent new diseases or symptoms. - Use follow-up     │
│  answers as the ONLY post-baseline evidence source. - An unchanged ranking      │
│  with an honest explanation is always correct. - Round all scores to 3 decimal  │
│  places.                                                                        │
│                                                                                 │

╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯

╭────────────────────────────── 📋 Task Completion ───────────────────────────────╮
│                                                                                 │
│  Task Completed                                                                 │
│  Name: You will receive the initial differential_diagnosis and the completed    │
│  questions_asked list with patient_answer fields filled in by the patient,      │
│  both provided as JSON blocks appended below this description by the runtime.   │
│  Also available: the disease_symptom_profiles list (which disease has which     │
│  candidate symptoms) from the follow-up payload.                                │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  WEIGHTED REFINEMENT SCORING ALGORITHM                                          │
│  ══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════         │
│  This algorithm uses the improved composite_score from Phase 1 as the baseline  │
│  score, then applies WEIGHTED follow-up evidence adjustments. Follow-up         │
│  symptoms that are more discriminative (appear in fewer candidate disease       │
│  profiles) carry more weight.                                                   │
│  ── Step 1: Compute discriminative weight for each follow-up symptom ──         │
│  Let N = number of diseases in disease_symptom_profiles with status "profiled"  │
│  For each question Q in questions_asked:                                        │
│    diseases_with_symptom = count of profiled diseases whose candidate_symptoms  │
│                            list contains Q.symptom (case-insensitive)           │
│    If diseases_with_symptom == 0: discriminative_weight = 0 (skip)              │
│    Else: discriminative_weight[Q.symptom] = 1.0 - (diseases_with_symptom / N)   │
│                                                                                 │
│  Examples with 5 profiled diseases:                                             │
│    - Symptom appears in 1/5 diseases: weight = 0.8 (highly discriminative)      │
│    - Symptom appears in 2/5 diseases: weight = 0.6                              │
│    - Symptom appears in 3/5 diseases: weight = 0.4                              │
│    - Symptom appears in 5/5 diseases: weight = 0.0 (not discriminative at all)  │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 2: Compute adjustments for each disease ───────────────────            │
│  For every disease D in initial differential_diagnosis:                         │
│    baseline = D.composite_score (from Phase 1)                                  │
│    support_delta = 0.0                                                          │
│    conflict_delta = 0.0                                                         │
│                                                                                 │
│    For each question Q in questions_asked:                                      │
│      Normalize answer: Q.patient_answer.strip().lower()                         │
│      w = discriminative_weight[Q.symptom] (or 0 if not computed)                │
│                                                                                 │
│      If answer is "yes" or starts with "yes":                                   │
│        If disease D's candidate_symptoms list contains Q.symptom:               │
│          support_delta += w    (weighted support)                               │
│                                                                                 │
│      If answer is "no" or starts with "no":                                     │
│        If disease D's candidate_symptoms list contains Q.symptom:               │
│          conflict_delta += w   (weighted conflict)                              │
│                                                                                 │
│      Any other answer → neutral, no change.                                     │
│                                                                                 │
│    final_score[D] = baseline + support_delta - conflict_delta                   │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 3: Re-rank ────────────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  Sort diseases by final_score descending. Break ties by match_count descending  │
│  (from Phase 1). Break further ties alphabetically. Renumber ranks starting     │
│  from 1.                                                                        │
│  ── Step 4: Confidence assignment ──────────────────────────────────            │
│  Let top_score = final_score of rank-1 disease,                                 │
│      second_score = final_score of rank-2 disease (or 0 if only one disease).   │
│      gap = top_score - second_score                                             │
│                                                                                 │
│  Rank-1 disease:                                                                │
│    HIGH   — gap ≥ 0.5 × top_score, or only one disease remains                  │
│    MEDIUM — gap > 0 but < 0.5 × top_score                                       │
│    LOW    — gap == 0 (still tied after all evidence)                            │
│                                                                                 │
│  All other diseases:                                                            │
│    MEDIUM — final_score > 0.5 × top_score                                       │
│    LOW    — otherwise                                                           │
│                                                                                 │
│  ── Step 5: Transparency ───────────────────────────────────────────            │
│  For each disease in the output, reasoning must explicitly state:               │
│    - Baseline composite_score from Phase 1                                      │
│    - Which follow-up symptoms were confirmed (yes) and their weights            │
│    - Which follow-up symptoms were denied (no) and their weights                │
│    - Net adjustment: +support_delta - conflict_delta                            │
│    - How the rank changed vs Phase 1 (e.g. "moved from rank 3 to rank 1")       │
│                                                                                 │
│  followup_summary must name the single most impactful answer (highest weight    │
│  confirmed or denied) and explain why it shifted the ranking.                   │
│  If ALL patient answers were neutral, set notes to:                             │
│    "All follow-up answers were neutral; ranking unchanged from baseline."       │
│                                                                                 │
│  ABSOLUTE RULES: - Only diseases present in initial differential_diagnosis may  │
│  appear in output. - Never invent new diseases or symptoms. - Use follow-up     │
│  answers as the ONLY post-baseline evidence source. - An unchanged ranking      │
│  with an honest explanation is always correct. - Round all scores to 3 decimal  │
│  places.                                                                        │
│                                                                                 │
